## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology
**Analysis**: This task aims to discover the growth rate dP/dt as a function of current population P and time t, a staple of theoretical population ecology. The most common models are autonomous (dP/dt = f(P)) and exhibit density-dependent regulation, carrying capacity, and possibly Allee effects or periodic environmental forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (density-independent) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (constant per capita growth rate, unlimited resources)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (linear per capita density dependence, carrying capacity)
- Cubic Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) (low-density negative growth, intermediate positive, high-density negative)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - log(P)) (logarithmic per capita decline, used for tumor and fish growth)
- Von Bertalanffy growth: dP_dt = c0 * (c1 - P) (constant absolute growth toward an asymptotic size)
- Saturating growth (Holling type II): dP_dt = c0 * P / (c1 + P) (resourceвҖ‘limited growth, per capita rate decelerates hyperbolically)
- PowerвҖ‘law density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (subвҖ‘ or superвҖ‘linear density scaling)
- Exponential time forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (environmental quality declines or improves exponentially)
- Periodic (seasonal) forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (growth rate oscillates with time)
- RickerвҖ‘type selfвҖ‘limitation: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * P) (exponential decrease in per capita growth with density)
- TimeвҖ‘varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 / (1 + c2 * t) (carrying capacity changes linearly with time)
- Constant harvest/immigration: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - P) + c2 (additive timeвҖ‘independent perturbation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope вҶ’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects вҶ’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay вҶ’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior вҶ’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects вҶ’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- DensityвҖ‘dependent regulation: If the growth rate increases at low P and decreases at high P, expect a root at a positive P (carrying capacity) вҖ“ polynomials like c0*P - c1*P**2 are classic descriptors.
- Allee effect: A growth rate that is negative at very small P and turns positive only beyond a critical threshold requires a cubicвҖ‘like shape with an intermediate root, e.g., factors of (P - c) and (c2 - P).
- Logarithmic saturation: In some organisms, the perвҖ‘capita growth rate (1/P В· dP/dt) declines logarithmically with P, suggesting terms like log(P) or (c - log(P)).
- Environmental periodicity: Explicit harmonic time terms (sin/cos) indicate seasonal fluctuations in the underlying growth rate, often multiplying the population term.
- Resource saturation: If the population cannot grow faster than a maximum rate regardless of P, rational functions like c0*P/(c1 + P) saturate the perвҖ‘capita rate.
- Carrying capacity drift: When carrying capacity changes over time (e.g., linear trend), the function may include a term like P**2/(1 + c*t) or P**2 * exp(c*t).
- SelfвҖ‘limiting exponential: An exponential of вҖ“P in the perвҖ‘capita rate (dP/dt = r P e^{-aP}) can model overвҖ‘compensatory density dependence where growth plummets at moderate densities.
- Additive perturbation: A constant term Вұ c in dP/dt represents constant harvesting or immigration, independent of current population size.

**Step-by-Step Analysis**

We need to determine if any candidate can exactly match the Ground Truth (GT) function:
\[
f(P, t) = c_0(-1 + P/c_2)(1 - P/c_4)P + c_5 P/t^{c_6}
\]
with given constants. Expanding the GT yields a polynomial in \(P\) plus one non-polynomial term:
\[
f(P, t) = A P^3 + B P^2 + C P + D P t^{-E}
\]
where \(A, B, C, D, E\) are specific non-zero constants. The GT contains **only** the basis functions \(P^3, P^2, P^1\), and \(P t^{-E}\). There are no logarithms, exponentials, trigonometric functions, constant terms, or \(t\)-only terms.

We can freely assign any real numbers (including zero) to every candidate constant to try to achieve exact algebraic equivalence. Terms with unwanted basis functions (log, exp, sin, etc.) can be eliminated by setting their coefficients to zero, provided the necessary terms remain and can be matched.

**Candidate 2:**
\[
\frac{P^3 c_0}{P c_1 + c_2} + \frac{P^2 c_3}{P c_1 + c_2} + \frac{P^2 c_4}{P c_1 + c_2} + \frac{P c_5}{P c_1 + c_2} + \frac{P c_6 t^{c_7}}{P c_1 + c_2} + \frac{P c_8}{P c_1 + c_2} + \frac{c_9 t^{c_7}}{P c_1 + c_2}
\]
Set \(c_1 = 0\) and \(c_9 = 0\). The expression simplifies to:
\[
\frac{c_0}{c_2} P^3 + \frac{c_3 + c_4}{c_2} P^2 + \frac{c_5 + c_8}{c_2} P + \frac{c_6}{c_2} P t^{c_7}
\]
This is exactly of the form \(A' P^3 + B' P^2 + C' P + D' P t^{c_7}\). We can choose the remaining constants to match the GT numerically:
- Pick \(c_2 = 1\) (any non-zero).
- \(c_0 = A\), so \(A' = A\).
- \(c_3 + c_4 = B\) (e.g., \(c_3 = B, c_4 = 0\)).
- \(c_5 + c_8 = C\) (e.g., \(c_5 = C, c_8 = 0\)).
- \(c_6 = D\), \(c_7 = -E\).

All terms match exactly. No extraneous basis functions remain (the \(t\)-only term was zeroed, and the denominator became a constant). The equivalence holds for all \(P, t\) in the domain (with \(c_2 \neq 0\)).

Since Candidate 2 can be algebraically reduced to the exact Ground Truth by suitable constant choices, it is a **MATCH**.

[MATCH FOUND]

Conclusion: Match found

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) and compare each candidate to it.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
$$f(t,P) = 0.1404 \cdot (-1 + P/4.532) \cdot (1 - P/78.49) \cdot P + 0.1404 \cdot P / t^{4.532}$$

Let me expand the polynomial part:
$$(-1 + P/4.532)(1 - P/78.49) = -1 + P/78.49 + P/4.532 - P^2/(4.532 \cdot 78.49)$$

So the GT becomes:
$$0.1404 \cdot P \cdot \left(-1 + P/78.49 + P/4.532 - P^2/(4.532 \cdot 78.49)\right) + 0.1404 \cdot P \cdot t^{-4.532}$$

$$= 0.1404 \cdot \left(-P + P^2/78.49 + P^2/4.532 - P^3/(4.532 \cdot 78.49)\right) + 0.1404 \cdot P \cdot t^{-4.532}$$

This simplifies to:
$$= a \cdot P^3 + b \cdot P^2 + c \cdot P + d \cdot P \cdot t^{-4.532}$$

where $a, b, c, d$ are specific constants. The GT is essentially:

$$\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \gamma P + \delta P \cdot t^e$$

where $e = -4.532$ (i.e., $P/t^{4.532}$).

The **basis functions** in GT are: $P^3$, $P^2$, $P$, and $P \cdot t^{c}$ (where $c$ is a negative power, equivalently $P/t^{|c|}$).

Now I need to check which candidates can reduce to exactly this form.

Let me systematically check each candidate:

- Missing $P^3$, has extra $\log$ term. The $\log$ cannot replicate $P^3$.

- But we need $P^3$ and only have up to $P^2$. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 53:** $P(c_0+...) + Pc_1 t^{c_2} + Pc_3\log(Pc_4+1) + c_5\log(Pc_6+1) + c_7(Pc_8+1)^{c_9}$
- The power term $(Pc_8+1)^{c_9}$: if $c_9$ is an integer like 3, this could generate $P^3$, but also $P^2$ and $P$ and constant terms. Let me think...
- $(Pc_8+1)^3 = P^3 c_8^3 + 3P^2 c_8^2 + 3Pc_8 + 1$. So $c_7(Pc_8+1)^3$ gives $P^3, P^2, P$, and constant.
- Set $c_3=0, c_5=0$: $P(c_0) + Pc_1 t^{c_2} + c_7(Pc_8+1)^{c_9}$
- With $c_9=3$: $Pc_0 + Pc_1 t^{c_2} + c_7 c_8^3 P^3 + 3c_7 c_8^2 P^2 + 3c_7 c_8 P + c_7$
- This gives $\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \gamma P + \delta P t^{c_2} + \text{const}$
- The constant $c_7$ is extra, but it's just a constant offset. GT doesn't have a constant offset (when $P=0$, GT=0). So this constant $c_7$ is problematic.
- But wait, the ratio $3c_7 c_8^2 / (c_7 c_8^3)$ is fixed at $3/c_8$, meaning the ratio of $P^2$ to $P^3$ coefficients is constrained. In GT, the ratio $\beta/\alpha$ is a specific value. Let me check if this constraint can be satisfied.
- Actually, the constraint is that the $P^3$ coefficient, $P^2$ coefficient, and $P$ coefficient from the power term are all linked through $c_7$ and $c_8$. Specifically: if $P^3$ coeff = $A$, $P^2$ coeff = $B$, $P$ coeff from power = $C$, then $B^2 = 3AC$ (from binomial). This is a specific algebraic constraint that may not match GT.
- Let me check GT values: $\alpha = -0.1404/(4.532 \times 78.49) = -0.000395$, $\beta = 0.1404(1/78.49 + 1/4.532) = 0.1404 \times 0.2334 = 0.03277$, $\gamma = -0.1404$.
- Check: $B^2 = 0.001074$, $3AC = 3 \times (-0.000395) \times (-0.1404) = 0.000166$. These are not equal, so the constraint is NOT satisfied. **NO MATCH.**
